## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard phase-space form of nonlinear oscillator ODEs. Common structures include restoring forces from potentials (linear, cubic, trigonometric), dissipative damping (linear/nonlinear), and external/parametric forcing in time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative restoring acceleration; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator with linear drag)
- Quadratic (speed) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag; dissipation grows with speed)
- Coulomb/dry friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (approximate dry friction; piecewise-nonsmooth dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness with linear damping)
- Pendulum (trigonometric restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (large-angle pendulum-like restoring from periodic potential)
- Sine + cubic correction: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * x**3 (mixed periodic and polynomial restoring; approximate complex potentials)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x| → limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent self-excitation and saturation)
- Driven oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance under periodic drive)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear damping + nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (higher-order corrections to restoring and dissipation)
- Potential-gradient form (generic conservative): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (acceleration from polynomial potential expansion; odd terms for symmetric potentials)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces often depend on x only (dv_dt ≈ f(x)); damping introduces v-dependent terms that remove energy over time.
- For symmetric potentials U(x)=U(-x), the restoring acceleration tends to be an odd function of x (terms like x, x**3, sin(c*x)).
- Hardening/softening behavior is indicated by adding x**3 (or higher odd powers), which produces amplitude-dependent frequency and nonlinear resonance shifts.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles typically appear as state-dependent damping, e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v, providing negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic driving is naturally represented by sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additions independent of (x, v), producing forced response and resonance peaks.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when x is multiplied by a periodic function of time, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, rather than adding a forcing term.
- Dry friction or impacts often create nonsmooth acceleration via sign(v), Abs(v), or piecewise forms, leading to stick-slip or sharp corners in phase portraits.
- Aerodynamic/turbulent-like drag often scales as v*Abs(v) (or higher odd powers of v), producing stronger dissipation at higher speeds than linear damping.
- Mixed polynomial + trigonometric restoring (e.g., sin(c*x) plus x**3) can indicate a periodic potential with anharmonic corrections or a truncated series approximation of sin.

GT: -beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3

GT (fixed) is:
\[
-2.5126990598325\,x^3\;-\;2.5126990598325\,x(0.0921849151045819\,t+1)\;-\;0.774919680656294\sin(v)
\]
So it contains exactly these term types (and nothing else):
- \(x^3\) with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\)
- \(x\) with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\)
- \(t x\) with coefficient \(-2.5126990598325\cdot 0.0921849151045819\)
- \(\sin(v)\) with coefficient \(-0.774919680656294\)
No standalone constants, no \(v\), no \(v^3\), no logs/exp/rational terms, no \(x^5\), etc.

Also, any candidate sine must be reducible to \(\sin(v)\) exactly for all real \(v\). That requires choosing parameters so that \(\sin(c3\,v+c4)=\sin(v)\) for all \(v\), which is possible by setting \(c3=1\) and \(c4=2\pi k\) (or \(c3=-1\) and \(c4=\pi+2\pi k\), etc.). So the sine part is matchable.

Now check candidates.

### 1. `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v + c6*t*x + c7*v*(c8 + x)**c9`
Has extra terms \(c5 v\) and \(c7 v (c8+x)^{c9}\) not in GT. Only way is set \(c5=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then it reduces to candidate 2 form, which can match (see #2).  
**Matchable** (by zeroing extra terms).

### 2. `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v + c6*t*x`
GT has no linear \(v\) term, so must set \(c5=0\). Then choose:
- \(c1=-2.5126990598325\)
- \(c0=-2.5126990598325\)
- \(c6=-2.5126990598325\cdot 0.0921849151045819\)
- Sine: set \(c3=1,\;c4=0\) and \(c2=-0.774919680656294\) (or any phase-equivalent choice giving exactly \(\sin(v)\)).
This reproduces GT exactly.  
**Matchable.**

### 3. `... + c5*x**5 + c6*v + c7*v**3 + c8*t*x`
Extra \(x^5, v, v^3\). Set \(c5=c6=c7=0\). Then it becomes same structure as #2 (with \(c8\) as \(tx\) coefficient). Can match by same parameter choices.  
**Matchable.**

### 4. Same as #3 plus `+ c9`
Extra constant term; set \(c9=0\) and also \(c5=c6=c7=0\). Then match as above.
